        function setCustomDimensions() {
            // Use set to persist page type so it is sent in all subsequent GA calls
            ga('set', 'dimension6', getPageType());  
  
            setTimeout(function() {
                if(getCookie("isUserRegistered")) {
                    var registrationStatus= getCookie("isUserRegistered");
                    if(registrationStatus === "true") {
                        ga('set', 'dimension1', 'Registered');
                    }
                } else {
                    ga('set', 'dimension1', 'Unregistered');
                }

                if(getCookie("isUserSubscribed")) {
                    var subscribedStatus= getCookie("isUserSubscribed")
                    if(subscribedStatus === "true") {
                        ga('set', 'dimension2', 'Subscribed');

                        if(getCookie("offerId")) {
                            var offerIdValue= getCookie("offerId")
                            if(offerIdValue) {
                                ga('set', 'dimension10', offerIdValue);
                            }
                        }
                    } else {
                        ga('set', 'dimension2', 'Unsubscribed');
                    }
                }
                else {
                    ga('set', 'dimension2', 'Unsubscribed');
                }
                ga('send', 'pageview', sinclairDigitalAnalytics.customDimensions);
            }, 500);
  
        }

family has seen the worst of its effects.{/p}{p}Her name was Callie Van Tornhout.{/p}{p}A life tragically cut short at just five weeks old.{/p}{p}&ldquo;She was too young for her vaccine, so she couldn&rsquo;t fight it. She was coughing, she was on life support,&rdquo; Callie&rsquo;s mom Katie Van Tornhout said. &ldquo;She was this brand-new baby fighting for her life, and there was nothing we could do to save her.&rdquo;{/p}{p}That heartbreak was caused by pertussis, also known as whooping cough.{/p}{p}Almost fourteen years later, her mother Katie spreads awareness of how communities can prevent children from getting the disease.{/p}{p}&ldquo;If you&rsquo;re not vaccinated as an adult, you can pass it on to an unvaccinated child unknowingly. In Callie&rsquo;s case, that&rsquo;s what happened,&rdquo; Van Tornhout said. &ldquo;She got it from a nurse who didn&rsquo;t know she was carrying it, and didn&rsquo;t have a Tdap booster, who passed it on to my daughter.&rdquo;{/p}{p}Dr. Jonathan Alterie said pertussis is highly contagious, so along with vaccines, many common strategies for germs apply.{/p}{p}&ldquo;If you&rsquo;re within six feet of someone who is coughing or sneezing, you can easily get pertussis. It also lives on surfaces for days on end,&rdquo; Alterie said. &ldquo;So, really just making sure that if you are ill &ndash; coughing or sneezing &ndash; cover your mouth, wash your hands.&rdquo;{/p}{p}Alterie said it&rsquo;s a good rule of thumb to take your child to a doctor if a cough persists for two weeks.{/p}{p}But if there are further symptoms, it could warrant a trip to the emergency room.{/p}{p}&ldquo;If the child is not eating or drinking, irritable and not acting themselves.             var firstTopStoryTagsArray;
    
            try {
                firstTopStoryTagsArray = sinclairDigital.facade.content['page-data'].teaser[0].teasers[0].tags;

                firstTopStoryTagsArray = [];

                    if (tagData["dimension"] === "Display" && tagData["name"] === "Major Story") {
                        isBreakingNewsPresentInFirstPosition = true;
                    }
                });
            }

class="StoryTags-module_listTagWrapper__hA5o"><p class="StoryTags-module_para__pyQi">TOPICS:</p><a class="StoryTags-module_storyTag__jAYb" data-index="0" data-tag-name="Whooping cough" draggable="true" href="/topic/Whooping%20cough">Whooping cough</a><a class="StoryTags-module_storyTag__jAYb" data-index="1" data-tag-name="Vaccine" draggable="true" href="/topic/Vaccine">Vaccine</a><a class="StoryTags-module_storyTag__jAYb" data-index="2" data-tag-name="Pertussis" draggable="true" href="/topic/Pertussis">Pertussis</a><a class="StoryTags-module_storyTag__jAYb" data-index="3" data-index="6" data-tag-name="Presque Isle County" draggable="true" href="/topic/Presque%20Isle%20County">Presque Isle County</a><a class="StoryTags-module_storyTag__jAYb" data-index="7" data-tag-name="Outbreak" draggable="true" href="/topic/Outbreak">Outbreak</a></ul></div><div class="StoryTags-module_tagWrapperLine__Jfav"></div><div class="StoryText-module_storyText__FWhP"><p>PRESQUE ISLE COUNTY, Mich., (WPBN/WGTU) -- It's highly contagious and it's impacting northern Michigan.</p><p>There are six confirmed cases of whooping cough in Presque Isle County.</p><p>District Health Department #4 said the patients are children under four years old.</p><p>UpNorthLive News spoke with a parent whose family has seen the worst of its effects.</p><p>Her name was Callie Van Tornhout.</p><p>A life tragically cut short at just five weeks old.</p><p>“She was too young for her vaccine, so she couldn’t fight it. She was coughing, she was on life support,” Callie’s mom Katie Van Tornhout said. “She was this brand-new baby fighting for her life, and there was nothing we could do to save her.”</p><p>That heartbreak was caused by pertussis, also known as whooping cough.</p><p>Almost fourteen years later, her mother Katie spreads awareness of how communities can prevent children from getting the disease.</p><p>“If you’re not vaccinated as an adult, you can pass it on to an unvaccinated child unknowingly. In Callie’s case, that’s what happened,” Van Tornhout said. “She got it from a nurse who didn’t know she was carrying it, and didn’t have a Tdap booster, who passed it on to my daughter.”</p><p>Dr. Jonathan Alterie said pertussis is highly contagious, so along with vaccines, many common strategies for germs apply.</p><p>“If you’re within six feet of someone who is coughing or sneezing, you can easily get pertussis. It also lives on surfaces for days on end,” Alterie said. “So, really just making sure that if you are ill – coughing or sneezing – cover your mouth, wash your hands.”</p><p>Alterie said it’s a good rule of thumb to take your child to a doctor if a cough persists for two weeks.</p><p>But if there are further symptoms, it could warrant a trip to the emergency room.</p><p>“If the child is not eating or drinking, irritable and not acting themselves. If the child is turning blue or not breathing, that’s called apnea, and they’ll get these spells of apnea. If they seem fatigued or you can see their belly going up and down, labored breathing – those are all signs that it’s time to go to the emergency room,” Alterie said.</p><p>DHD #4 offers Tdap and Dtap vaccines at clinics in Alpena, Atlanta, Cheboygan and Rogers City.</p><p>Contact your doctor or health department in your area for more information.</p></div></div></div></div><div
